Establishment of the Chinese Hygiene Society

Adoption of the Charter and Election of Directors

Central Committee member Chu Minyi and Health Minister Liu Ruiheng initiated the organization of the Chinese Hygiene Society. The inaugural meeting was held last night at Xinghualou. Chu Minyi was publicly elected chairman to report on the development of the society. In a short time, 134 people signed up to join the ranks of the founders. The charter was then discussed, and directors were elected. Chu distributed the draft charter he had prepared to the members for public discussion. Wang Wanbai stood up and said that the draft charter was generally sound, but as it was a national society, the number of directors should be increased to fifteen to cover distribution, and proposed that the first directors be nominated by the founders to save time. Yu Fengbin stood up to second. The proposal was put to a vote and unanimously approved. Next, the directors were mutually nominated. Minister Liu Ruiheng announced the list of fifteen directors, including Chu Minyi, Quan Shaoqing, Wang Wanbai, Xiao Zhiji, Zheng Hao, Niu Huisheng, Xu Naili, Pang Jingzhou, Yan Fuqing, Hu Hongji, Wang Qizhang, Cai Yumen, Chen Wanli, Fang Zhao, and Liu Ruiheng. Chu Minyi was appointed to convene the first board meeting. Thus, the Chinese Hygiene Society was declared established in a round of applause. The adopted charter is recorded below:

Charter of the Chinese Hygiene Society (1) Name: The name of this society is the Chinese Hygiene Society. (2) Purpose: The purpose of this society is to develop the science of hygiene, revitalize the hygiene industry, and seek the health of the Chinese people so that they can enjoy a healthy life. (3) Organization: A. The founders of this society are the natural members of this society. B. All hygiene experts, members of the new medical community, and people from all walks of life who agree with the purpose of this society may become members of this society upon the recommendation of two members of this society. C. This society shall have fifteen directors, who shall be elected by the general meeting of members for a term of two years and may be re-elected. D. This society shall have one president and two vice presidents, who shall be elected by the directors. E. Those who are particularly enthusiastic in supporting this society may be publicly nominated by this society as honorary president or honorary directors. F. This society shall have two departments: the General Affairs Department, the Public Relations Department, and the Publicity Department. Each department shall have one director, who shall be concurrently held by the directors. There shall be a number of secretaries. The detailed rules of each department shall be determined separately. (4) Membership fees: All members shall pay an admission fee of two yuan upon joining, and then pay an annual membership fee of four yuan. Those who are willing to donate especially are particularly welcome. (5) Expenses: The expenses of this society, in addition to admission fees, annual membership fees, and special donations, may be raised temporarily when there is a shortfall. (6) Meetings: A. The board of directors shall hold an ordinary meeting once every six months, which shall be convened by the president. A general meeting shall be held at least once every two years. When necessary, a temporary general meeting may be convened by the board of directors or at the request of ten or more members. B. This society may establish branches in various places. The charter shall be formulated by the branches themselves with reference to the charter of the general society and shall be approved by this society. (7) Address of the Society (to be determined by the board of directors) (8) Supplementary Provisions: If there are any imperfections in this charter, they may be discussed and amended at any time by the board of directors.

Request for the Issuance of Regulations on the Prohibition of the Import of Medical Contraband

Municipal Government Letter to the Ministry of Health

The Shanghai Special Municipality Health Bureau previously stated that the measures for prohibiting the import of medical contraband had not yet been issued, resulting in many inconveniences in handling procedures. It specially submitted a report to the Municipal Government, requesting the Ministry of Health to issue the measures as soon as possible. After receiving the report, the Municipal Government yesterday sent a letter to the Ministry of Health, stating, "For the matter of requesting a letter, according to the Health Bureau, the imported syringes and injection needles used for medical purposes are originally needed for treating diseases. There are often shameless people who use them for other purposes, which is harmful to society, which is not shallow. All countries have regulations to ban the import of such needles. In Shanghai alone, the number of such needles imported and smuggled in each year is quite large. If they are not strictly restricted, it will not be enough to stop the flow. For example, recently, the German merchant Sin Yi Chemical Pharmaceutical Company imported as many as 800 dozen of such needles. The Public Security Bureau repeatedly sent letters asking whether it could be allowed to extract all of them. The bureau believes that this matter is important and there are no special regulations to rely on. It immediately replied to the bureau that it can only temporarily follow the provisions of Article 5 of the Sino-German Agreement on the Prohibition of Anesthetic Drugs, that if such needles are to be transferred to other places for sale, they should be handled in accordance with that article. If they are not transferred to other ports, but are to be sold in Shanghai, since there is no need for such a large number of needles in Shanghai, only two-tenths can be received, and then two-tenths can be reported after the sales are completed. When reporting for the second time, the names of the people to whom the needles were sold and the signature and seal or signature of the buyers must be sent to the bureau by the company for review and verification before the second batch can be reported to make a temporary transition. There are also foreign merchants and foreign firms who privately order such needles from foreign countries. After arriving at the port, they cannot extract them from the customs, and have to sell them to hospitals or doctors, hoping to have the names and seals of hospitals or doctors so that they can extract them. Unexpectedly, the customs must rely on the bureau's letter to verify before they can extract them, which has caused foreign firms to entrust doctors or hospitals to submit requests for certification. All of this is because the regulations have not been issued, resulting in many inconveniences in handling procedures. In order to make it easy for the public, it is requested that you review and approve the submission to the Ministry of Health, and that the regulations on the prohibition of the import of such needles be formulated and promulgated as soon as possible, so that there is a basis." Based on this, the claims of the bureau are true, and it is appropriate to request your ministry to verify and handle them and reply.

Local News

Criminal Arrest in Zhenru District, Jin Lane: Gamblers Resist Police

Hooligans Gather Gamblers, Villagers Gather a Crowd of a Hundred People to Stubbornly Resist

Village Chiefs Report, Police Chief Leads Forty Police to Surround and Arrest

Sixteen Gamblers Arrested

Seven Officers and Police Injured

Yesterday morning around 3:00 AM, a villager resistance incident occurred in the third jurisdiction of the fourth district of Zhenru Town. When the local police went to Jin Lane to arrest gamblers, they were suddenly confronted by more than one hundred villagers holding weapons such as pistols, Mauser pistols, broadswords, iron and wooden clubs, hoes, and axes. They fired sixty or seventy shots, injuring six officers, including the inspector. Numerous firearms, silver dollars, badges, and uniforms were seized. It was not until dawn that sixteen criminals were captured. The details are as follows:

Three Gambling Dens: Zhenru is located eighteen miles northwest of Shanghai. Most of the residents are farmers, and policing is difficult due to the long reach. During the Lunar New Year, local thugs and hooligans often gather crowds to gamble, profiting from skimming, which is extremely harmful. However, their movements are very secretive, and they are well-prepared, making it difficult to arrest them. Therefore, they have become even more unscrupulous recently, with as many as three gambling dens.

Director Yang Reports: Yang Pinzhi, the director of the town, could not bear to stand idly by as the gambling trend intensified. He submitted a report to the police station of the third division of the fourth district at 9:00 PM the night before, requesting that police be sent to apprehend them.

Pursuit and Gathering Crowds: After receiving the report, Director Yang immediately ordered Inspector Cheng Yankun, Sergeant Liu Weibei, and police officers Sang Wanqing and Bai Junqing to proceed to Jin Lane at night with flashlights, badges, and other items to make arrests. While traveling near the Shuixiang Temple, about eight miles from the town, they encountered four villagers. One of them was holding a child and was dressed extravagantly. Inspector Cheng suspected their behavior and ordered them to stop and submit to questioning and inspection. The villagers replied, "We are returning from a wedding feast and do not need to be searched." The inspector, considering their rude remarks, stepped forward to stop them. Unexpectedly, two of them suddenly ran away. This increased their suspicion, and they pursued them on foot. However, due to the darkness, the three disappeared in an instant, and the fourth took out a police whistle and blew it wildly. In no time, villagers gathered upon hearing the sound, creating a clamor of gongs and drums. In a few minutes, the crowd grew larger and larger, reaching about one hundred people, some holding pistols and Mauser pistols, others wielding broadswords, iron and wooden clubs, or carrying hoes, axes, and bamboo poles. They surged forward in a tumultuous manner, shouting, "Charge! Beat them to death!" The sound reached several miles.

Villagers Stubbornly Resist: The police officers, outnumbered, did not resist at all. Inspector Cheng, fearing that the situation would escalate, ordered the police to report back to the director while he climbed to a high place and earnestly advised them, "We are here to arrest gamblers, which is to eliminate harm for the people. You are all law-abiding villagers. Why are you resorting to violence? Anything can be discussed." However, the villagers were unreasonable. Those with guns fired continuously, sounding like strings of beads. After about ten minutes, they ran out of ammunition and resorted to using knives and clubs. At this critical moment, Inspector Cheng ordered the police not to retaliate but to hide in the low-lying areas to avoid danger. However, many were injured as a result.

Armed Arrest: Half an hour later, Director Yang led more than forty police officers, armed with live ammunition, to suppress the situation. The villagers, seeing the situation, knew they were no match and scattered like birds and beasts. The police then bravely surrounded and arrested twelve criminals. However, the injured were numerous, lying on the ground unable to move. The captured criminals were escorted back to the station. However, when they were about two miles from the station, a large group of villagers came from behind, intending to seize them. The director ordered the police to fire several shots into the air to scare them away and then moved forward to apprehend them, capturing four more and bringing them to the station.

Names of Those Arrested: According to the interrogation of those arrested, Ayou is from Jiading, 46 years old, living at Zhuyang Bridge; Qian Yongcai, 28 years old, living at Luoyang Bridge, runs a rice store; Chen Chunsheng, 22 years old, living at Chenjiazhai; Qian Bosheng, living at Luoyang Bridge, 30 years old; Qian Xitang, 48 years old; Qian Laoyu, 29 years old; Qian Quanlin, 22 years old; Qian Jisheng, 31 years old; Qian Fangchu, 32 years old; Qian Amao, 36 years old; Qian Jinping, 54 years old; Qian Jiang, 21 years old, all living at Luoyang Bridge; Feng Atong, 47 years old; Qian Weiquan, 22 years old; Chen Chunwang, 22 years old; Qian Genyuan, 23 years old, all from Jiading.

Police Officers Injured: As for the police officers, Inspector Cheng Yankun suffered a head injury, a fractured left arm, and lost twelve silver dollars, a party certificate, a wallet, and other items. Sergeant Liu Weibei and police officers Sang Wanqing, Bai Junqing, Shi Zaisi, Huang Lisheng, and Wang Futing were all injured in the head, arms, and body. Cheng and Sang suffered the most severe injuries. They were all sent to the Baolong and Jisheng hospitals for treatment. A large number of seized firearms and uniforms were also recovered.

Japanese Woman Confesses to Killing Japanese Child

Theft Due to Poverty... Murder Due to Theft

Wenhui News reports that the seventeen-year-old dancer Niye, who brutally murdered the one-month-old daughter of Kajiwara Sadashichi, was arrested last night (the 10th). This morning (the 11th), she confessed to Chief Hanari at the Japanese consulate that she committed the murder due to theft and signed the confession. In the afternoon at 4:00 PM, she was taken to Judge Aoki for questioning and temporarily detained. She will be transferred to the Nagasaki District Court for preliminary hearing within a week. According to her confession, she is seventeen years old and came to Shanghai from Dalian on the 28th of last month. She worked as a dancer in a certain bar on North Sichuan Road. However, her income was not sufficient, and her stepfather was unable to assist her. She left after a few days, intending to find another place to live. Last Saturday, she visited a friend on Dixiwei Road but did not find them. On her way back, she saw the gate of No. 807 ajar, and no one was around. She thought to herself that she had no money and was starving, and the landlord was pressing her to pay rent. Now was a good opportunity to sneak in and steal a few items from the hat rack to pawn and use. After entering, she saw that there were only a few men's hats on the rack and nothing of much value. The house was quiet, and she became bolder. She crept upstairs and into a room, where she saw a baby sleeping soundly. She found a set of manicure tools and several pieces of jewelry, such as rings, in a box, as well as several pads. As she was tying them with a ribbon, the baby suddenly woke up and cried. She initially tried to comfort the baby by patting its face and holding its hand to stop the crying, but it was ineffective. She then pressed the pads and other items on its face, but it continued to cry. She then tied its throat with a white cloth, but it was still ineffective. At that moment, there were footsteps downstairs. She was very anxious and killed the baby with the manicure tools. She cannot remember how she did it at the time, but she knew she closed the manicure tools and hurried out of the room, running down the stairs. She remembered encountering Mrs. Kajiwara at the top of the stairs, who asked her what she was doing. She pushed her aside and fled, hiring a rickshaw to return to North Sichuan Road. It is also said that this woman suffered from mental illness.

1929 Detective Team Work Achievements

Since the appointment of Qiao Songsheng and Ying as captains of the Municipal Public Security Bureau Detective Team, they have made tireless efforts in rectification, achieving remarkable results. According to detailed investigations, the team cracked a total of 241 cases of kidnapping, reactionary activities, intimidation, theft, abduction, gambling, and other cases in 1929. In January of this year, they also successively solved theft cases in Hengfeng Road, Junhe Lane, Zhihe Lane, Chongde Lane, and other places, as well as kidnapping cases involving the young master of the Huayangchi family on Hengfeng Road and the Zou family's son on Zhoujiaqiao Road in Wusong. The number of cases solved is as follows: 1. Kidnapping: 24; 2. Theft: 60; 3. Reactionary activities: 8; 4. Communist Party activities: 10; 5. Abduction: 36; 6. Larceny: 38; 7. Intimidation: 18; 8. Gambling: 10; 9. Other cases: 17. Total: 241 cases.

Dalun Lease Termination Case Appeal

Dalun Real Estate Company and Da Zhonghua Department Store Co., Ltd. entered into a lease agreement in the autumn of the year before last, leasing the area of thirty-odd shops owned by the former, stretching from the post office on Nanjing Road to Hibiya, to the latter to build a grand twelve-story department store. It was found that the leases for each shop were indefinite. In early November of the year before last, Dalun had once declared to the shops that it had leased the area to Da Zhonghua Company and notified them to terminate their leases in early September of last year. Because the tenants refused to move out, Dalun filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai Provisional Court. In the first instance, on November 20 of last year, a judgment was made ordering the defendants to move out within a specified period. Subsequently, the defendants' representatives, lawyers Zheng Yuxiu and others, declared an appeal. The plaintiff, citing the prolonged delay of the case and significant losses, has entrusted Lian Kui, Shi Ying, Li Zuyu, He Qingyun, and other lawyers to appear in court to argue against the appeal. It is heard that the case is scheduled to be heard by Hu Yigu, the president of the appellate court, on the 12th of this month.

Hua Dawei Bigamy Case to Be Pronounced

Hua Dawei, a native of Changzhou, was sued by his first wife, Yang Yonghua, in the Provisional Court for bigamy. The first hearing was held a few days ago, but the defendant did not appear, while his second wife, Tang Manqi, appeared in court to testify. It was ordered that Hua Dawei be summoned to court for further questioning. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge held a continued hearing, and both parties appeared. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, the plaintiff's accusation is based on the defendant's bigamy, not on the 3,000 taels of gold stipulated in the agreement. Yang Yonghua further stated that her husband and Tang Manqi were married at Xuyuan Park, and her in-laws attended the wedding, but she did not. The agreement was signed at the end of March of the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, under duress from Dawei. According to the defendant Hua Dawei, he is now twenty-three years old. He had an old-style wedding with Yang Yonghua in his hometown fifteen years ago. The following year, he came to Shanghai and studied at St. John's University. Through the introduction of a friend, he met Miss Tang and developed a romantic relationship. Later, with the mediation of relatives from both sides, this agreement was established. He then had a new-style wedding with Tang at Xuyuan Park on the sixth day of the fourth month, with his adoptive father as the officiant. He and Tang now have one child each. The 3,000 taels of gold in the agreement have been paid to the plaintiff by his parents. However, due to urgent needs, he had borrowed 300 yuan from the plaintiff. When he became involved with Tang, he was only twenty years old, so she did not suspect that he already had a wife, and he did not say it directly. It was not until he returned to Changzhou during the summer vacation that Miss Tang learned the truth. According to Tang Manqi, when they fell in love, Hua only said that he had parents and sisters, but not a wife. She said that she would never have married him if she had known he had a wife. After returning to Changzhou after the wedding at Xuyuan Park, she learned that he was already married, but it was useless to make a fuss, so she returned to Shanghai after a week. Her parents then questioned Hua, who said he would find a way to divorce Yang. She now wants to sue Dawei as well. After mutual arguments by the lawyers of both parties, Judge Ge ordered that a date be set for the pronouncement of the judgment.

[P Zhao Hongen Inducement Crime>

Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Zhao Hongen from Anhui Province induced Ke Baidi (also known as Xingbao, sixteen years old), the daughter-in-law of Zhu Dehe from Hubei Province, who resided at No. 183 Tongxing Lane, Yangshupu Road, to the Zhongnan Hotel on Aivenyi Road for illicit cohabitation and defrauded her of her clothing. After someone reported it to the Xinzha Patrol Station, detectives arrested Zhao and the suspect Liu Jinsheng and brought them to the Provisional Court for interrogation. This was reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Luo held a continued hearing. Ke's husband, Zhu Yuqing, and his father, Zhu Dehe, both appeared in court, requesting that Zhao be severely punished, and stated that if she was willing to return home, they would take her in. Ke stated that she now wished to enter the Jiliang Institute. After reviewing the case, Judge Luo found that Zhao Hongen had induced a woman under the age of twenty to leave the custody of her parents and should be punished according to the law. He sentenced him to six months imprisonment. Liu Jinsheng was found not guilty. Ke Baidi was released to the custody of her grandfather, Zhu Dehe, for supervision.

Rapid Theft in Wusong

The owner of Wang Yushun Salted Goods Store on Doushi Road in Wusong, Wang Asan, lives at No. 135 Xian Road. His wife, Wen, locks the door after dinner every evening and takes the children to her brother-in-law Wang Ayuan's house across the street to chat by the stove. Unexpectedly, thieves arrived the night before. After Wen left, the thieves first twisted the door of Wang Ayuan's house with wire and then pried open the door of Asan's house and entered. They went straight upstairs to Wen's bedroom and stole a valuable jewelry box from the dressing table drawer, containing three pairs of gold bracelets of various sizes and gold rings, weighing more than twelve taels in total, as well as banknotes and silver dollars worth one hundred yuan. The thieves immediately fled after obtaining the items. Their movements were extremely fast, taking less than thirty minutes. When Wen returned home and saw that the front door was open, she was very surprised and suspected something was wrong. She went upstairs to check and realized that a theft had occurred. She immediately informed her husband, Asan. Upon inspection, fortunately, 600 yuan in silver dollars stored in another drawer had not been stolen, which was fortunate in misfortune.

Cai Wang, a woman from Xiamen residing at No. 2241 Peng Road, had recently suffered from mental illness. Man Suffering from Mental Illness Cuts His Throat

Xu Hongzhang, a 23-year-old native of Ningbo, resided at No. 1080 Huade Lane, Huade Road, Hongkou. He was unmarried and worked as a painter at the Telephone Company. He had suffered from mental illness since last spring, with occasional flare-ups. Around 3:00 AM yesterday morning, he was sleeping in the room with his father when he suddenly woke up and got out of bed, muttering to himself. He reportedly said, "Someone at the company is talking about me, dismissing me from my job, and sending police to arrest me and take me to the court for trial." He grabbed a pair of scissors from the table and stabbed himself in the throat, about an inch deep. He bled profusely. His father woke up from the noise and saw Hongzhang covered in blood, with the scissors still in his throat. He quickly removed them and hired a streetcar to take his son to Tongren Hospital for treatment.

Not Wanting to Quit Smoking, Swallowed Smoke

Wasted a Life

Wang Cai, an elderly woman from Tianjin residing at No. 441 Tangshan Road, Hongkou, scolded her son, Wang Guozhen, for being addicted to opium around 8:00 AM the day before yesterday. She urged him to quit smoking, but he did not listen. Angered, she secretly swallowed opium smoke to commit suicide. Her family discovered this and transported her to a nearby hospital for treatment, but she died. The hospital, in accordance with regulations, notified the Huishan Patrol Station, which sent detectives to transport the body to the Philand Road Mortuary. The Provisional Court commissioned Judge Gao Junxiang to come to the mortuary yesterday morning at 11:00 AM and determined that she had committed suicide by swallowing smoke. He ascended the judgment seat and questioned the deceased's son, Wang Guozhen, and found no other circumstances. He ordered him to sign a guarantee and take the body for coffin preparation.

Unruly and Wild Adulteress

Repeatedly Escapes for Secret Encounters

Finally Arrested Together

Cao Shiting, a native of Ningbo, is nearly forty years old and works as a driver at Central University in Wusong. His wife, Cao Yu, is thirty-two years old. The couple used to live in Lanni Ferry, Pudong. However, Cao Yu is naturally promiscuous and became inextricably involved with Zhu Jiangde, who is in his twenties. Disliking her husband's incompetence, she ran away in December 1927. She was found and brought back twice. Cao then moved to Huaanfang in front of the City God Temple in the city. However, she ran away again. She was found and brought back after a month and moved to Yangjia Tomb Hill in Pentang Lane. In June of last year, she ran away again. Before long, she was found again by Cao at the end of the year. He brought her to live in Maijia Lane, Wusong. Unexpectedly, she ran away again after only seven days, claiming to be going to a relative's house. However, Cao knowingly allowed her to leave, secretly waiting by the roadside. He saw her walk a few steps and then meet her lover, Zhu Jiangde, and walk away together. Cao secretly followed them and saw the couple go into the Zhonghe Hotel. Cao then went to fetch his younger brother and alerted the police to search the premises. They were found together in Room 4 and arrested and taken to the Seventh District Police Station. After interrogation by the judicial branch, they were transferred to the local court for trial yesterday.

Failure to Repay Debt Results in Mob Violence

Zhou Shaoliang, a 23-year-old native of Changzhou, is currently unemployed in Shanghai and temporarily resides with a friend at Yaojia Stone Bridge in Zhabei. Last year, he and his friend Zhang Genrong jointly opened a Dexingguan snack bar near the Xiangwu Stage in Zhabei. Due to differing opinions, they transferred the business to Zhang alone during the Mid-Autumn Festival in August, with Zhang agreeing to pay Shaoliang 100 silver dollars as compensation. Zhang's brother, whose given name is Genrui, opened a Dashun Hotel at the North Railway Station and asked Zhou to temporarily lend him the 100 yuan, with interest accruing at a rate of two cents per month. Zhou reluctantly agreed out of consideration for their relationship and immediately drew up a loan agreement as proof. In October, due to financial difficulties, Shaoliang asked Zhang for 20 yuan to cover living expenses. The remaining money has not been returned to date. Wu Zhou went to collect it every few days, but Zhang always prevaricated and did not return any of it. Yesterday evening, three hooligans, Lin, Shen Duofu, and others, came to Zhou's residence, falsely claiming that Boss Zhou had ordered them to inform him that his money would be available at a certain teahouse in Hongzhen tonight. Zhou went there on time and soon saw the three young men, Lin and the others, enter, but Zhang Genrui did not come. As soon as he sat down, the three men took out three axes from their clothes and, without asking why, struck Zhou's head twice with the axes, fracturing his skull. They struck his back once, his left arm once, and his left hand once. He collapsed, bleeding profusely. The assailants then disappeared without a trace. Villagers helped him hire a rickshaw to take him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. It is said that Zhou's injuries are extremely critical.

Pudong Electric Company Changes Date for Suspending Daytime Electricity Supply

This Month, the Sixteenth Day

The Pudong Electric Company began supplying daytime electricity on May 1, 1929. However, due to equipment issues, it was stipulated that the supply would be suspended for one day each month on the 1st and 16th, National Day, and other public holidays for maintenance and repairs. Considering that many factories are closed on Sundays, for the convenience of users, it is proposed to change the method, starting from February 16, to suspend daytime electricity supply every two weeks on Sundays. It submitted a revised business charter to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau for approval. The bureau believed that although the period of this change was shorter than the originally scheduled suspension of electricity supply on the 1st and 16th of each month, most factories that use electricity are closed on Sundays, so suspending electricity at the same time would not have a significant impact. Also, both parties would have convenience in repairing machinery and equipment, so it was presented to the municipal government for approval.

Datong Music Society's New Arrangement of Seasky Music

Entitled Ice Flowers and Snow Moon Chapter

The Shanghai Datong Music Society held its first concert of the year last Sunday. It began with the National Grand Music, followed by songs such as Spring River Flower Moon Night and Rainbow Feather Dress. The director of the society, Zheng Jinwen, gave a welcome speech to the guests. Zhang Ziyu then said that there are many ancient famous songs in our country, all in the musical scores. Why not select the best and translate them? Zheng agreed with his words and decided to translate the ancient Seasky Wind qin music into a large-scale ensemble. The entire work has twelve sections. Because the melody is cold and captivating, without any sense of worldliness, it was named the Ice Flowers and Snow Moon Chapter. Retaining its original name, it is called Seasky Music. After discussion by the members, for the sake of precision, Zheng first drafted the work, dividing it into four categories: wind, strings, plucked instruments, and percussion, and issued them to specialized members, allowing each to fully utilize their strengths, freely add embellishments or break down characters, but without changing the character of the music to create a separate score. Then, they would be combined into one and a general score would be written, with a deadline of two weeks for submission and rehearsals starting in four weeks.

Wusong Electricity Users' Declaration

Wusong merchants have organized a United Electricity Users Association to demand that Baoming Electric Company reduce electricity charges, and have stopped paying electricity bills for January, which has not yet been resolved. Yesterday, the association widely distributed leaflets, stating in essence: The reasons for organizing this association are: 1. The electric meters used by Baoming Company are very inaccurate in terms of rate, faster than those in Shanghai, and exploit users; 2. The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company has already reduced electricity charges starting in January of this year, but Baoming Company remains the same, charging 23 cents per degree, a difference of five cents, which is an enormous difference. The number of units of electricity used by users each month has a limit of at least ten units per month. If only seven units are used, the electricity bill for ten units must still be paid, which is more unfair than anything else. The association's goals are: 1. Reduce electricity charges; 2. Abolish the limit; 3. Calibrate the meter; 4. Provide daytime electricity.

Applauding the Arrest of Mongolian Road Robbers

City Public Security Bureau, Decree No. 86 of the Legal Department, states: In order to inform about a case reported by Inspector He Yun and Deputy Inspector Yang Rong, stating that Inspector Liu Yunfang reported a robbery at the home of Xiao Yuan of Jinkang Lane, Mongolian Road, Fourth District, First Precinct. They immediately rushed to investigate and, according to the victim Xiao Yuan, at around 7:00 AM that morning, while still in bed, three robbers suddenly broke into the house. One, wearing a short black cotton-padded jacket and carrying a handgun, demanded to know the location of money and valuables, forbidding any outcry. One of the robbers woke Ms. Xiao and forcibly removed a jade ring from her finger. They then ransacked drawers and boxes for about thirty minutes. Finding nothing of value, they stole a wristwatch from a small drawer. Fortunately, a relative, Lin Rongfa, saw that only two robbers had left, and one remained inside unarmed. Lin bravely closed the door, grappling with the remaining robber. Ms. Xiao then instructed her sister to call the police. The police took the robber to the station, where, according to Station Chief Ni, the robber confessed his name was Chen Qianbao and identified his two accomplices as Zhou Yongsheng and Wang A'da, both residing at 54 Nanxing Road. Upon receiving this confession, the Station Chief dispatched officers to the address and apprehended Zhou Yongsheng. Wang A'da had fled upon hearing the news and remained at large. Upon receiving instructions, the findings of the investigation and a sketch map were submitted for review. Based on this, the findings were compiled and submitted for review. In view of this, it was found that Ni Wenbiao, Station Chief of the First Precinct, Fourth District, had submitted the apprehended robbers, Chen Qianbao and Zhou Yongsheng, to the Bureau after the robbery at the home of Xiao Yuan in Jinkang Lane, Mongolian Road. After interrogation, the suspects confessed to the robbery. The case has been submitted to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for further interrogation. These robbers, daring to conspire and wield weapons, disturbed residents in the early morning, intimidating and robbing them before attempting to flee. Such behavior is extremely unlawful. The relative, Lin Rongfa, stepped forward in a moment of crisis, bravely apprehended Chen Qianbao, the remaining robber indoors, demonstrating both courage and intelligence. He is commended and awarded twenty yuan in silver to be distributed to him as a reward for his bravery. The victim, Xiao Yuan, a woman facing robbery in a moment of distress, was able to instruct her family to sound the alarm, alerting nearby police officers. Her alertness and awareness are commendable and rare. Station Chief Ni Wenbiao, upon receiving the report, immediately discovered the robbers' address and quickly apprehended the accomplice Zhou Yongsheng. His prompt action is also commendable. In addition to instructing the station to proceed accordingly, this order is hereby issued to the district and precinct captains for dissemination to all personnel for their information. This decree is issued by Director Yuan Liang on February 11th, 19th year of the Republic of China.

Yesterday morning, Judge Tan Xinzhen continued the hearing. Xu maintained his innocence, stating he had no involvement in the kidnapping. crew members Cao A'san, Zeng Debing, Zhu Daoshun, Cui A'san, Xu Lu Lin, Cui Anren, Cao Gong, Pang Dalong, Yang Gui, Xu Zhi, and others, totaling twelve people, were taken along with the two boats to the Lujiazui Water Police Station. Inauguration of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's Commodity Inspection Conference in Beijing

The first day of the Commodity Inspection Conference convened by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce was the day before yesterday. At 7 AM, Vice Ministers Zheng and Mu, along with all members, paid respects at the Mausoleum. At 9 AM, the opening ceremony was held in the meeting hall of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Attendees included Chen Tianjing, Zou Bingwen, Zhang Fengwu, Wu Chengluo, Gao Bingfang, and dozens of others. Vice Minister Zheng presided, with Rong Yehou and Shen Guojin as recorders. After the formalities, Minister Kong, on sick leave, sent Secretary Chen Duan to represent him and deliver an address, briefly stating: 1) The Commodity Inspection Bureau is not a tax collection agency, and its name should reflect reality, emphasizing inspection rather than revenue; 2) Emphasis should be placed on research to improve product standards and promote export trade; 3) It should be commercialized rather than bureaucratized; 4) Diligence, caution, integrity, and honesty should be the guiding principles of service. Vice Minister Zheng delivered a speech, briefly stating: 1) This conference is the first of its kind in China's industrial and commercial administration; 2) Your decision to pay respects at the Prime Minister's Mausoleum before the meeting is a sincere expression of accepting the Prime Minister's teachings; 3) China has not valued commodity inspection in the past, leading to repeated failures in the credibility of exported goods; 4) The Ministry's implementation of commodity inspection is to restore international trade credibility and the inherent national [honesty in commerce] ethics; 5) It is hoped that the experience of the past year will be shared and discussed in the conference. Then, Vice Minister Mu instructed Director Zhang Yiou to deliver a speech. Finally, the meeting adjourned with refreshments.

Fire in Yangshupu Road This Morning

Couple Both Burned

A straw shed opposite the Samsung Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road caught fire accidentally at 1:30 AM this morning. The fire quickly spread through the roof and became a raging inferno. The couple inside were awakened from their sleep and escaped from the fire, but both suffered severe burns. The woman was near death. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade rushed to the scene to extinguish the fire. The injured were taken to the scene by Western police officers from No. 295 and transported to Tongren Hospital for treatment.

Relief Efforts of the Jisheng Society for the Shaanxi Famine

Report from the Xi'an Branch

The Chinese Jisheng Society yesterday received a telegram from Lu Junhe, of the Jisheng Society's Xi'an branch, stating that since winter and the twelfth lunar month, Shaanxi province has experienced continuous heavy snow and severe cold unprecedented in decades. The famine victims have already torn down their houses for fuel and are now trapped in snow caves, without fire. They are either dying of hunger or cold. Entire families are freezing and starving to death, buried in the ice and snow. The disaster is so dire that it is unbearable to witness. The General Society has already established numerous shelters in Xi'an, Wugong, Qishan, and other counties, accommodating thousands of elderly, weak, women, and children, and the relief funds are substantial, but the Society's resources are stretched. The Xi'an shelters are full and unable to accommodate more people. There are still elderly, weak, women, and children in need of aid, waiting to die. Therefore, it is imperative to request the addition of two more shelters to save them from death. The Society has been working on relief efforts in Shaanxi for years, expending a great amount of funds. Now, the Society has taken on the tasks in Zhejiang province's Taizhou, Wenzhou, Linning, etc., Ping province's Nankou, Zhaizang, Mentougou, Anhui province's Xuanzhou, Wuhu, etc. Relief efforts in one province are already difficult, let alone several. However, the Society cannot abandon the elderly and weak awaiting death in Xi'an. Therefore, the Society cabled Xi'an yesterday, approving the addition of two shelters, limited to one thousand people, excluding the elderly, weak, women, and children already awaiting death. It was reported that the Society's relief efforts in Shaanxi are ongoing, and additional assistance is being provided to several provinces, including Zhejiang, Ping, and Anhui. The disaster is widespread, and resources are stretched to their limit. It is hoped that philanthropists will contribute resources to alleviate this suffering, as the disaster victims in all provinces are relying on the Society's efforts.

Indigo Dye Workers Urge Cloth Industry to Increase Allowance for Drink Money

Indigo dye workers in this city, feeling the strain of rising prices and the difficulty of making a living, have requested an increase in drink money from the Cloth Industry Association. After many days of no response, the Shanghai Indigo Dye Workers' Union sent a letter to the Cloth Industry Association yesterday, stating: "We are writing to inform you that our union members, feeling the hardship of life, proposed on February 4th to your association that drink money be increased appropriately. The amount requested may seem large on the surface, but it is not excessive in proportion to current prices. In short, the cloth and dye industries are interconnected. Although our colleagues are just laborers, they understand the big picture. Would they only care about their own benefit and not consider the benefit of others? However, it has been eight days and your association has not given a definite reply. It is a pity. If your association has any difficulties, you should frankly report and discuss it fairly. Your Association's disinterest is unacceptable. Due to the workers from each factory asking after this matter, another letter has been issued with the hope of a prompt and complete answer. (The rest omitted)"

Record of the Coal and Charcoal Industry Congress

The Shanghai Coal and Charcoal Industry Guild held a congress yesterday morning at 9 AM. The attendees agreed that the current economic tension in society has severely impacted the industry. Last year, twelve businesses closed down, accounting for over one-fifth of the total. It is imperative to discuss and salvage the situation. The following resolutions were made: 1) Regarding the case of a certain steamer damaging industry rules: It was resolved that when the steamer arrives in Shanghai, the industry must wait for a temporary notice from the guild before unloading. 2) Regarding the discussion of increasing commissions: It was resolved to temporarily retain the matter and handle it when the opportunity arises. 3) Regarding the reorganization of industry regulations: It was resolved that the payment term for each shipment of goods is one month, and the payment will be 98% cash upon pickup. As for Wenzhou drafts, payment will be made upon sight of the draft when the goods arrive, with a five-day delay, treated as cash payment. This will be implemented on March 1st. It was also resolved that the guild will engrave industry regulations and a seal with the inscription: "Industry Agreement, 98% Cash Upon Pickup, Advance Payments Not Included." 4) Regarding industry members increasing commission: It was resolved that the industry will provide a commission of 0.2%. This will be implemented on March 1st. Supplementary resolution: The deposit issue will be handled according to the resolution of February 4th. The meeting adjourned at 12 PM.

Bandit Song Debiao Sentenced to Five Years in Prison

The bandit Song Debiao, colluded with a gang and used weapons to rob Fan Rongkun's home on Route Paul Henry in the French Concession. Detective Jin Jiulin, detective Li Yaolong, deputy detective Mao Jingen, bao detective Zhou Buguang and Shen Jinshu of the special agency of the French Concession Police Station investigated the case. They apprehended Song and his concubine Yao, confiscated a pistol and dozens of bullets, and brought them to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the French Court for trial. The plaintiff described the robbery. Song Debiao confessed to the robbery. Song's concubine Yao claimed that she had known Song for only a short time and was unaware that he was a bandit. The court sentenced Song to five years in the French prison, after which he would be deported. Yao was released without charge. The pistol was confiscated.

Handball Game at the Central Sports Field

Players' Performance is Remarkable

The Central Sports Field on Avenue Joffre and Route Amiral Bayle has been open for over seven days. Because of the novelty of the ball game, there are many spectators. However, many people do not understand the true meaning of the ball game. According to an internal staff member, this kind of ball game depends entirely on sharp eyesight and great strength. Skill and intelligence are equally important. At first glance, it is not very interesting, but upon careful observation, the wonderfulness of the skills is amazing and inspiring. The game is divided into single matches, double matches, and special matches, etc. In a single match, one person competes against another. In a double match, two people form a team, and one team competes against another.

Rules of the game: The playing field is surrounded by walls on three sides and divided into fifteen squares. The fourth square is called the "fault line," and the seventh square is called the "inner court line." Players must serve the ball by hitting it hard within the frame on the front wall. When the ball returns to the fourth square, the opponent catches it with a rattan basket worn on the right hand and hits it hard against the wall again. Then, the two sides take turns hitting the ball back and forth. If one side fails to catch the ball, they lose one point. According to the rules, the ball must be caught after bouncing on the ground once to be valid. If the ball bounces twice before being caught, the player loses one point and is out of the game. Each match uses a round-robin system. For example, if the first player plays the second player and the second player loses, the first player then plays the third player. The players fight in a circuit until one of them scores five points to win. Another example, a single match of five players means the first to get five points wins. A doubles match of six teams, meaning first to six points wins. And so on. There are also exceptions: special games that must get 20 points to win.

Dates of the Games: The fifth round of games has now been changed and scheduled for Friday and Saturday nights at 9 PM. There will be two games on Sunday, one at 3 PM and one at 9 PM.

New Publication Forthcoming from the White Goose Painting Society

Preparations for the White Goose Art Weekly

The renowned art group, the White Goose Painting Society, has recently been preparing a pure art weekly, named "White Goose." The format and content are extraordinarily splendid. The entire book is printed on coated paper with exquisite printing. Text, pictures, and photography are equally important. In addition to Chen Qiucao, Fang Xuegu, Pan Siyue, and Du Xuehou, the responsible members of the association, who are responsible for editing each section, more than ten famous artists from Shanghai are specially invited to contribute to each issue. Editing has already begun, and the publication is scheduled to coincide with the opening of the third exhibition of the White Goose Painting Research Institute on the 20th of this month. It will be sold at major bookstores, newsstands, and theaters both locally and abroad.

Robbery Log

Zhoujiazui Road: At 9:40 AM yesterday, two robbers broke into No. 3330 Zhoujiazui Road. One held a handgun and forbade anyone to make a sound. They stole 16.4 silver yuan.

Avenue Haig: At 9:05 AM yesterday morning, two thugs, both armed with handguns, broke into No. 1351 Avenue Haig in the International Settlement, threatening and intimidating the occupants. They searched and robbed clothing and cash, totaling 570 silver dollars.

Park Road: At 3:30 AM yesterday morning, a pedestrian was walking along Park Road when six or seven bandits, one armed with a knife and one with a handgun, blocked his way. They stole a fur coat, a watch, and over ten silver dollars before fleeing.

Rue Tenant de la Tour: Around noon yesterday, four robbers broke into the home of Ms. Zhang Chen at No. 13, Rue Tenant de la Tour, in the French Concession. Two of the robbers held handguns and forbade anyone to make a sound. They stole a fur coat and gold jewelry, worth approximately 250 yuan, before fleeing. The victim reported the incident to the police.

Baoyu Lane: Wei Lishan, from Huangyan, Zhejiang, formerly opened the Gong Taixiang foreign goods store at Xiaobeimen and lived at No. 74 Baoyu Lane, Market Street, French Concession. Around 11 PM the night before last, four robbers speaking with a local accent suddenly arrived. Three of the robbers had handguns and forbade anyone to make a sound. They drove all the occupants of the house into the back room upstairs. Each robber carried more than a dozen two-foot-long strips of white cloth, which they used to tie up all the adults and children and gag their mouths. Then they ransacked the house for about half an hour before escaping with their loot. After the incident, a detailed examination revealed that 54 silver dollars and 150 paper dollars had been stolen, along with twelve gold rings and gold ornaments such as buttons, hairpins, and bracelets, totaling about 1,150 yuan. The victim reported the theft to the Big Bell Police Station, requesting investigation.

The Shanghai National Products Factories United Association sent a letter to the Zhabei Yangguang Local Miscellaneous Dye Donation Office yesterday, stating: "On January 8th of this year, members of our association, the Guangming Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Co., Ltd., prepared to ship two boxes of Resolute Brand cold and hot thermos bottles to Little Luzon on November 23rd, 18th year, when an inspector from your office stopped them at Doushan Road, Zhabei, ordered them to pay a donation, and seized the goods, which have not been returned yet. Commercial Press Sells Almanacs

The 150-year Yin-Yang comparison almanac, which was proofread by the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau and the Director of the Education Bureau, has been sold throughout Shanghai since its publication. The contents can be used to check the correspondence between the Yin and Yang calendars and the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches for 150 years, so that dates on birthdays, anniversaries, and old bills and contracts can be recalculated according to the National Calendar, making them clear and easy to understand. It is the only almanac to supplement the abolition of the Lunar Calendar. The Commercial Press and the Civilization Bookstore are the general distributors of the book, which sells for only 60 cents per copy.

Criminal Instructions: Shang Haishan is the defendant for illegal private detention and public slander. (Principal Text) For officials whom the administrative officer deems necessary to dismiss or punish, but is concerned about the leakage of information, leading to desertion or destruction of evidence, the emergency measure of custody and inspection is within the supervisory authority and should not be considered illegal private detention. The publication of an official's conduct or criminal facts and the reasons for custody are a necessary procedure, and cannot be considered slander. Since the allegations are not criminal facts, the self-accusation is rejected. Above February 11.

Shanghai Local Court

Public Notice: Regarding the public notice of the auction, this court is executing the case of creditor Zhu Taotao, etc., and debtor Wang Lushi due to a debt lawsuit, and has sealed the real estate owned by the debtor Wang Lushi, and the minimum price has been set. The auction will be held at the entrance of this court on February 26. The first round of bidding will open on March 4. All residents who wish to purchase this real estate should submit their name, age, place of origin, address, and occupation, and clearly state the price they are offering. The sealed bids should be submitted. The auction will open on the due date in accordance with the law, and the bidder with the highest price will be the successful bidder. The successful bidder shall pay one-fifth of the bid price as a deposit on the same day, and the remaining amount shall be paid in full upon delivery. The court will issue a property certificate. If the payment is not made by the deadline, the bidder with the next highest price will be selected, and the procedure will be repeated. Free Talk

Mourning Mr. Yu Huizun

-- Wu Yancheng

Mr. Yu Huizun, a respected elder of the Six Heng Village in Dinghai. His given name was Zhaoxiong, and in his later years, he went by the alias Weicun. During the Qing Dynasty imperial examination era, scholars focused solely on examination essays and were unwilling to study the classics and history, leading to criticism for their lack of substance. Mr. Yu alone enjoyed reading ancient books. His poems, prose, and lyrics drew heavily on the classics and history, embodying their essence and beauty, and were widely admired by scholars at the time. During the county and prefectural academy examination periods, he would occasionally submit his work and always ranked at the top. However, talent is often met with adversity. Despite repeated recommendations, he never passed the higher-level examinations and remained a senior licentiate for life. The people of the town admired Mr. Yu's learning and competed to hire him to teach their children. Therefore, many gentlemen, merchants, and people from all walks of life in Shanghai today are his students. He had a literary friendship with my late uncle, Mr. Ziyu, and they were the closest of friends. Our family also hired him to teach and provided meals, so I was also one of his students. Mr. Yu was short-sighted and kept his hands on his books at all times, which eventually led to blindness in his later years. Mr. Yu was morally upright and gentle in nature. He never argued with others and did not like to hear about external affairs. The inhabitants of the isolated island of Six Heng mostly worked in fishing and salt production, and there was a lack of educational seeds. Mr. Yu's learning and writing were respected by the villagers, and he was publicly elected as the village head. However, this was not what Mr. Yu desired. The islanders had limited knowledge and did not understand any new policies. Others were responsible, but they focused their criticism on Mr. Yu. The seventy-year-old man sacrificed himself. His entire family of four also died for Mr. Yu. Alas, the rioters killed him and then burned his house. How cruel! More than ten years ago, I often corresponded with Mr. Yu, but recently, due to mundane matters, we had not been in contact for a long time. When the terrible news arrived, I could not help but cry aloud. Alas, why does Heaven not bless good people? Or is Heaven about to abandon culture?

News Clippings

— From Tōkyō

The Tōkyō Times depicts an angel. Its right hand holds a watch, symbolizing the swift passage of time. Its left hand holds a mirror, signifying clear and illuminating insight. The newspaper's unique quality captures elegance completely. The initial letter "K" of the Boston Morning Journal is drawn as a postman, also uniquely charming. Our newspaper adopts the wooden bell (Mù Duó) as its emblem. Heaven intends for the teacher (Confucius) to be the bell, with a deep meaning of alerting the masses.

In Paris, the so-called "Three-Line Classifieds" can bring each newspaper 50,000 francs. The annual cost of telegrams for the Japanese News Alliance's Chinese intelligence is approximately 100,000 pounds.

Honeymoon Insurance

— Jī Jìn

According to Western customs, after a wedding, the couple must travel together to famous scenic spots or major cities, which is called the honeymoon. According to a friend, the Parker & Company in New York, USA, is established for this type of insurance. They usually focus on various newspapers. Upon seeing a wedding announcement, they will send someone to persuade the newlyweds. If the new couple agrees and designates the destination, all travel by boat or car, as well as food and accommodation, can be handled at any time. The insurance premium is very cheap, divided into ordinary and special types. It is said that the ordinary type costs only two shillings per person per day. If an accident occurs, the company will immediately compensate for the loss according to the regulations. This is also an innovative insurance method.

A Laughing Matter

— Hǎi Kè

A: Girl, their love is extremely deep. They made a vow, saying it would be "forever unchanging."

B: Girl, then have they gotten engaged?

A: Girl, fortunately, love is eternal, so it's not too late to get engaged in two thousand years.

Son: Father, how many major rivers and mountains are there in Asia?

Father: I don't quite understand this.

Son: Father, you really lack knowledge. When the teacher asks me tomorrow, I will be scolded.

A: Tomorrow is your grandfather's funeral. Of course, you have to hold the rope and accompany him.

B: As long as it doesn't rain or the wind doesn't blow, I will certainly accompany you.

Professor A: Every morning, students are often late. Saying more is useless. It really makes me helpless.

Professor B: I have an excellent method.

Professor A: I would like to ask for advice.

Professor B: Be late yourself.

A: Lovers breaking up is really the best thing ever.

B: Why?

A: Look, my lover and I have been arguing for a week. Haven't we saved more than ten dollars?

A recent newspaper magazine carried a drawing titled "The Future of a Journalist." Eyes like Yama (the king of hell), like a thousand-mile eye. Ears like Bajie (Pigsy), like all-hearing ears. Head with horns. Spine with fins. The left hand is a writing brush. The right hand becomes a draft paper. Feet with wheels. Moves like flying. Water, land, and air, without obstruction. It is said that in the future, one must be like this to fully realize the ability of a journalist.

The country with the most widespread newspapers in the world is Denmark. It has 3,200 daily publications, 750 periodicals, and a total circulation of 1.11 million. The national population is 3.4 million. On average, one newspaper is read per three people.

A Trip to Boluo in Guangdong

— Mǐn Hǎi Bó Yá

There is a Cantonese saying, "First, marry a wife; second, travel to Boluo." These two phrases are thought-provoking. When I traveled to Boluo, I realized that it does indeed have the same flavor as marrying a wife.

Boluo County is in the east of Guangdong. In the middle is the Hongsheng Temple. Every year on the thirteenth day of the first month, it is the saint's birthday. The incense is very prosperous. During the late Qing Dynasty, there was a royal sacrificial ceremony. Therefore, the custom of traveling to Boluo has not disappeared to this day. Every year on this day, people come and go at the ferry, and men and women are like clouds, endless. And "Boluo Bathing in the Sun" is one of the Eight Scenic Spots of Yangcheng. The temple is located on the mountainside. Looking into the distance, the sunlight rises from the opposite sea. Its glow and the waves reflect each other, almost making one feel as if one is in Fusang (Japan). It is truly worthy of being one of the Eight Scenic Spots of Yangcheng. Below the temple, there is a shallow sandy beach, about two zhang (approximately 6.67 meters) from the shore. The water only reaches the ankles. However, the tourists are neatly dressed. Who would be willing to walk barefoot? This has become a speculative business for ordinary "pearl ladies" (young women). On this day, the pearl ladies all dress up beautifully, wear shorts, and make a living carrying people across the shore to the temple. Their income is indeed substantial, and it also allows those who are carried to taste the flavor of "chicken head meat" (a slang term for being taken advantage of). The saying that marrying a wife is likened to traveling to Boluo refers to this.

On that day, the temple sells a large quantity of paper chickens, called Boluo Chickens. Those who return from traveling to Boluo must carry one in their hands, saying that this may bring good luck for the year. It is also said that immortals personally visit the area every year, such as the Wang Yeren (a legendary figure) disguised as selling glutinous rice balls. Those with immortal bones can ascend to immortality by eating these glutinous rice balls. It is also said that Lü Chunyang (a Taoist immortal) also used magic to sell paper Boluo Chickens every year. Among them, there must be one that can crow and herald the morning. These are all strange tales from Qi State. Just listen to them casually.

Two Interesting Anecdotes

— Sōng Bīn Tīng Tāo Kè

A few days ago, on the Beijing-Shanghai train, the long journey was boring. I happened to hear a passenger chatting and learned two interesting anecdotes. Some may think they are fictitious, but the narrator spoke with certainty, and it didn't seem like fabrication. Because the matter is quite interesting, I recorded it in writing to submit it to this column.

Resourceful Couple: In a residence on Xiafei Road, Xiafei Lane, two thieves suddenly visited one day. One thief, holding a Browning pistol, entered the room first, threatening the people inside to hand over the key to the safe. While the man was hesitating, his wife calmly said to the thief, "Don't hurt anyone. The key can be given." Then she told her husband to go and get the key. Seeing this, the thief thought they were cowards, so he held the gun and followed the man. The wife also followed behind the thief. The thief didn't pay attention to her because she was a weak woman. Unexpectedly, in an instant, the wife suddenly kicked the thief's elbow holding the gun with her foot. The gun fell to the ground. The thief was shocked and didn't know what to do. The wife immediately stepped forward and firmly grabbed him. Her husband also quickly turned around, picked up the gun, and aimed it at the thief. The thief dared not move. Looking at

Red Carpet

A Record of Watching Xun Huisheng's "Fragrant Silk Ribbon"

— Lǎo Zhuō

On the evening of the seventh, I watched a performance at the Grand Theatre. The main act was "Fragrant Silk Ribbon," one of Xun Huisheng's finest new plays. The plot is very similar to the Bangzi opera "Three Suspicious Plans." However, "Three Suspicious Plans" ends with an apology. After the apology in this play, it continues with Tang Tong's expedition, where he encounters thieves at an inn. He is bound with a fragrant silk ribbon, beheaded, and his body is abandoned. This leads the crowd to suspect the corpse is Tang's. The police even falsely accused Tang's wife and her relative, Du, of adultery. Fortunately, Tang's teacher has already passed the imperial examination and was appointed as an investigating censor. When touring this county, he reviewed the case and suddenly recalled the midnight knocking on the door years ago. He forcefully ruled it as a case of adultery and murder. When they were about to be executed, Tang returned, and the injustice was cleared. The second half of the play's plot is quite similar to "Selling Er'e After Cutting off Her Feet." It is difficult for new plays to escape the conventions of old plays. They are generally similar. But speaking of the play itself, Tang's wife, Lin, played by Huisheng, is forced by her husband to knock on Lu's teacher's door late at night. And the police falsely accuse her and her relative, Du, of adultery and murdering her husband. Undeserved misfortune, suffering alone. Writing the intangible sorrow is more difficult than writing the tangible sorrow. The author maintains a quiet and virtuous attitude throughout, which is very consistent with the identity of the character in the play. And the performance is neither impulsive nor following the trend, but only a sense of infinite sadness. The so-called heart is ten times more bitter than the autumn lotus. Huisheng is really good at portraying the characters. The singing, starting with the Xipi San Yan in the first scene, contains new melodies, which is exceptionally beautiful. The song "Urging Makeup," in Er Liu meter, is melancholy in its lyrics, and so is the singing. In the courtroom, the eight sentences of the Fan Er Yao Ban have ever-changing melodies. No beats are more difficult than having beats, but this is Huisheng's specialty. Listening closely, Huisheng's voice is fine, but the articulation is extremely clear. The inflections and releases, the light and heavy, fast and slow, are all in harmony with the rhythm and achieve perfection. This shows the sharp progress of her skills over the years. Assisted by Zhang Chunyan as Tang Tong, the rude man; Jin Zhongren as Lu Shike, with a strong scholar's air; and Ma Lu as Du, the rogue of the city, they are all suitable for their talents and deserve to be called excellent performances.

the wind, the thief outside peered in and raised his Browning pistol, and could only surrender. The narrator said that the couple must be skilled in martial arts. Otherwise, how could they be so brave?

Accidental Encounter with One's Own People: Doctor A knew a ruffian named B and had treated him before. One night, Doctor A was walking alone in an alley, wearing a thick coat and hat. Suddenly, he encountered someone stripping him bare. While struggling, he saw in the lamplight that it was someone he knew. Doctor A smiled and said, "Now I've met my own people. What will you do?" B was ashamed and couldn't answer. Doctor A untied his pouch, gave him some coins, and left.

Chì Sōng Zǐ (Red Pine Nut)

— Jūn Měi

Yesterday at the spring banquet of Mr. Wang, I recognized a dish. Its taste was fresh and delicious, with a sour fragrance that permeated the lungs. It was wrapped in yellow mud and called Chì Sōng Zǐ. Because of its shape, all the guests, old or young, didn't know what it was after a quick gamble. They were surprised that they had never tasted it before and didn't know how to eat it. They asked Mr. Wang. Mr. Wang said, "It's not difficult. You can remove the mud with bamboo chopsticks and open the paper. First, suck the soup. Then remove the shell and eat it with vinegar. It should have a wonderful taste." So the guests were eager to try it. The sound of bamboo chopsticks, breathing, and shell cracking mixed together. Everyone thought it was a miraculously delicious dish. They asked to describe the method. Mr. Wang said, "This is a family dish. The method is to take a raw egg, grind a small hole, and inject shrimp meat, add soy sauce, and add Ajinomoto (MSG). After the inner layer is complete, seal the hole with hard paper, spread chili sauce on the shell, soak it in a vinegar bowl for three or four minutes, take it out and store it in a bowl, and steam it. It's cooked. Its taste is as good as delicacies from land or sea." I recorded it when I returned home. The aftertaste is still there. Not wanting to keep it a secret, I recorded it to share with like-minded people.

Wit Born of Desperation

— Shuāng Dāi

If a man is harassed by prostitutes in the middle of the road and cannot get rid of them, he only needs to say softly, "I have sores all over my body." They will definitely let go and leave. I have tried it many times and it has always worked.

When cashiers of money shops or inns are escorting silver dollars (this method does not apply to those wrapped in cloth or rattan baskets) and encounter bandits robbing them along the way, they should loudly pretend to say, "There are military supplies in the bag… I hope you don't misunderstand." When the thieves hear "military supplies," they will hesitate and not dare to act immediately. Then shout loudly, "Military supplies!" to easily attract the attention of passers-by and detectives, and you may be spared.

Warmth in the Heart (127)

— Bāo Tiān Xiào

Chapter 8: The Delicate Birds Sing and the Flowers Bloom at the Qióng Feast / The Golden House is Decorated, and the Good Bird Chooses the Wood

Zuǒ Shīchén said, "I heard that the madams in the brothels often beat and scold people they keep… Have they ever beaten you?" Ruǐyún said, "Scolding is unavoidable, but I've never been beaten. I've suffered a lot. Besides my parents, this 'Big Aunt' (madam) has been the best to me. Because my business has been very good since I started working. Now, I have to sing thirty or forty songs every day. Of course, they also make a lot of money off of me. So, she naturally flatters me, calling me 'sweetie' all the time… But if I have a few days with fewer songs or a week without any customers, she'll pout and scowl. Even if she doesn't say anything, I know she's unhappy. Even when I call to her, she answers listlessly, as if she's not responding. But it's still good, because I've suffered so much in these few years. Compared to that, it's not too bad… I can tell you in detail about it another day." Zuǒ Shīchén was about to ask her how she was sold from her family when he saw the Big Aunt come out. She said, "Sweetie, dinner is already served in the pavilion. I specially told them to cook the grass that you like to eat… Young Master, you're welcome to come and sit in the pavilion, too." Zuǒ Shīchén followed her in. Ruǐyún then took Shīchén's hand and said, "Today, I saw your friend, Zheng Seven Young Master, who is always at the racetrack across the street… I ran into him at the Yiqingxian Pavilion. He even asked about you, saying, 'Has Second Young Master Zuǒ called?'" Shīchén said, "Who is hosting the party at the Yiqingxian Pavilion?" Ruǐyún said, "It's someone named Xu. Everyone calls him 'Special Photo'… Big Aunt, why do they call him 'Special Photo'? Is that kind of nickname?" Shīchén said, "Special Photo means a handsome face. Because Shanghainese call the face a 'photo.' For example, to ask if someone's face is good-looking, they'll say, 'Is his photo new?' Now that they're calling him 'Special Photo,' he must have a handsome face." Ruǐyún said, "Yiqing dressed up as a man today and looked very good… Someday, I want to dress up as a man, too." The Big Aunt said, "Yiqing is taller than you. She looks good dressed as a man. You're shorter than her. Men's clothes won't look good on you." Ruǐyún said, "Today, Yiqing wore a foreign-style hunting cap… She arranged beads into the two characters 'Yiqing' and fastened them on the hat. Everyone said she looked good. Tomorrow, I'll arrange beads into the two characters 'Ruǐyún' and fasten them on the hat… or put them on a small melon-cap… That would also be special." Shīchén said, "That kind of special… You'd also become a 'Special Photo.'" Ruǐyún rolled her eyes at Shīchén and continued, "You always say I wear that kind of beaded veil… It's old-fashioned… It's not popular now… I look like a little old lady." The Big Aunt said, "The weather is getting warmer… You don't need to wear a beaded veil anyway."

Gold Price Rises Again

Silver Prices Fall, Exchange Market Tightens, and Public Sentiment Shows Optimism: Yesterday, February 11th, the price of gold rose again, probably because the overseas silver market has fallen again and the exchange rate is also tending to tighten. Colleagues have tried to buy in, but the buying and selling within each market vary, but there is no large number of transactions. Most people are bearish, but the major players are holding steady. Judging from the current market situation, it is difficult for prices to rise significantly. However, the period is during the spring sales season, and if all parties develop formally, the yarn market may rebound. The spot sales are expected to be cleared out, and pure futures are trending downwards. For the sake of stability, customers are temporarily standing by and waiting for the right moment. The future of the yarn market is still in a process of change.

There is a lack of improvement in the bid for yarn. At the opening of the morning session, the spot price rose along with the rise in foreign cotton, and the situation was more tense. The Origin of High Cotton Prices

American Cotton Rebounds... Hankou Customers Go Long

The cotton market has stabilized. The telegram from American cotton showed a rebound. The local market atmosphere is upward. Due to the high land prices, Hankou customers are buying large quantities of cotton futures in the futures market, so the market price has slightly increased. However, the spot cotton sales are not very prosperous. This is because the factories have already ordered a lot of Indian cotton. There is no urgent need for local cotton at present. However, some people think that the consumption of American cotton has decreased and they are bearish. Japanese short sellers have also closed their positions. The future of the cotton market may be unstable for a while.

The Hankou Bid Rebounds by 0.04-0.05 Yuan. At the opening of the morning session of cotton futures, the selling pressure in the market decreased greatly due to the rebound of American cotton by 0.3-0.4 pounds. Retail investors scrambled to hedge, and the prices of all months rose by 0.04-0.05 yuan. In the second and third sessions, long positions were closed, and the market suddenly fell by 0.02-0.04 yuan. As a result, it only rose by 0.01-0.02 yuan. In the afternoon, the market situation was slightly stronger due to the buying of Hankou customers, and the prices of all months rose by 0.025-0.03 yuan. The total turnover for the day was 41,900 dan. The closing prices of the Hankou bid are recorded on the left.

Sources of Silk, Tea, Lu Huang, and Grey Warp Have Stopped

Due to Qingdao Implementing Local Goods Export Public Scale Tax

Yellow Grey Silk Warp is a special product of Shandong Province, which has always been shipped from Qingdao and Yantai to Shanghai by wheel, and sold to various foreign firms by Shanghai-based banks for export. Recently, the source of Yellow Grey Silk Warp suddenly stopped, and Shanghai Zhuang telegraphed the place of origin for inquiries. Now receiving a reply telegram roughly says that this is because the Qingdao authorities have implemented the local goods export public scale tax, and the business community has risen up to oppose it, while the official office insists on its implementation, so they have temporarily suspended business and transportation in an attempt to resist it. It is feared that it will be difficult to ship Yellow Grey Silk Warp for a while.

Recent Automobile Numbers in Shanghai by Ding Zuze

According to the automobile registration numbers at the Traffic Department of the British and French Municipal Councils in this city, the number has increased by 20% in the past year. This progress can be said to be rapid. On January 1st of last year, the total number of registered automobiles in the two concessions of this city, including passenger cars, trucks, and motorcycles, was 10,167. On January 1st of this year, the total was 12,380. In addition, the business permits for cars tested in the county are not included.

Among the above-mentioned 12,380 automobiles, there are approximately 400 different brands. Among them, about 20 of the most famous brands can be identified. The number of these 20 brands accounts for almost half of the total.

There are about 15 automobile dealers in this city. Most of the brands they sell are Ford, Chevrolet, Buick, Morris, Chrysler, Flyer, Citroen, Renault, and Austin. In addition, there are several dealers selling trucks and motorcycles.

Judging from the above-mentioned numbers, the increase in the past year is 2,213 vehicles. However, this is contradictory to the actual situation. In reality, the automobile dealers in this city sell no more than 2,000 new cars each year. And only two companies sell the most: one sells about 700 vehicles, and the other sells about 500 vehicles per year.

However, according to the automobile dealers, there is another reason. In recent years, most automobile sales involve trading old cars for new cars. After purchasing a new car, the owner simply hangs the old license on the new car and does not re-register with the Municipal Council. If the old car is still sold in this city, then this second owner will find that one more car is added when registering with the Municipal Council. However, most old cars traded for new cars no longer appear on the roads of this city. Some of these old cars are transported to the interior, some are discarded as useless, and some cannot be sold. If the number of imported cars from the customs is used as a basis, it is also not accurate, because the imported cars are not all sold in Shanghai. Therefore, it is indeed not easy to investigate the number of new cars added in this city each year.

Now, a table is listed below to show the detailed numbers of various vehicles registered in the two concessions on January 1st of the past two years:

British Concession　　French Concession

1929　1930　1929　1930

Private Passenger Cars　4171　4783　2613　3078

Commercial Passenger Cars　393　541　342　465

Private Trucks　615　701　528　648

Commercial Trucks　498　833　241　489

Motorcycles　624　737　142　115

From the above table, except for the decrease in motorcycles in the French Concession, all types of vehicles have increased.

Furthermore, regarding the famous automobiles in this city, Buick cars have been the most numerous in previous years. At its peak, there were a total of 982 vehicles. Unfortunately, it has decreased to 941 vehicles three months ago. Ford cars and Morris cars have been making rapid progress. This year, the leading position will be occupied by Ford cars or Morris cars. Chevrolet cars are also a rising star. According to the registration of passenger cars, there are currently 825 Ford cars, 794 Morris cars, and 625 Chevrolet cars. On October 1st of last year, there were only 778 Ford cars, 772 Morris cars, and 591 Chevrolet cars.

The following table lists the famous automobiles in this city in order of quantity:
